# Custom Config Files | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Custom Config Filesarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)

**Last Modified:** Friday, January 9, 2026 at 12:01 PM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#overview)

Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide details how to create and register custom configuration files for your Hytale plugins using the server's **Codec system**. Configuration files allow users to customize your plugin's behavior without modifying code.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#what-are-config-files)

What are Config Files?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Configuration files:

*   Store plugin settings in JSON format
    
*   Allow users to customize plugin behavior
    
*   Persist across game sessions
    
*   Use Hytale's Codec system for serialization/deserialization
    
*   Auto-generate with default values if missing
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#understanding-the-codec-system)

Understanding the Codec System


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Hytale uses **Codecs** to serialize (save) and deserialize (load) data:

*   **Codec:** Defines how data is converted to/from JSON
    
*   **BuilderCodec:** Fluent API for building complex codecs
    
*   **KeyedCodec:** Maps a JSON key to a Java field
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#step-1-create-the-config-class)

Step 1: Create the Config Class


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The configuration class acts as a data model that defines:

*   Variables to be saved in JSON
    
*   How they are serialized/deserialized
    
*   Default values
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#basic-config-class-example)

Basic Config Class Example:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#understanding-the-codec-builder)

Understanding the Codec Builder


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Let's break down the codec definition:

*   **First parameter:** The config class type
    
*   **Second parameter:** Constructor reference (how to create new instances)
    

*   **KeyedCodec:** Maps JSON key to field
    
*   `"LuckIncreaseChance"` - JSON key name
    
*   `Codec.DOUBLE` - Data type codec
    
*   **Setter lambda:** How to set the value when loading
    
*   **Getter lambda:** How to get the value when saving
    

*   **add():** Finalizes the current field
    
*   **build():** Completes the codec
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#step-2-register-in-main-plugin)

Step 2: Register in Main Plugin


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For the server to recognize and load the configuration file, register it during plugin initialization:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#configuration-file-location)

Configuration File Location:

The config file will be generated at:

**Format:** `{Group}_{Name}/{ConfigName}.example.json`

Where:

*   `Group` and `Name` come from your plugin's `manifest.json`
    
*   `ConfigName` is the first parameter to `withConfig()`
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#multiple-configuration-values)

Multiple Configuration Values


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can add multiple fields to your config:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#common-codec-types)

Common Codec Types


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Java Type

Codec

Example Value

`Double`

`Codec.DOUBLE`

`0.40`

`Integer`

`Codec.INT`

`100`

`String`

`Codec.STRING`

`"Hello"`

`Boolean`

`Codec.BOOL`

`true`

`Long`

`Codec.LONG`

`1000000L`

`Float`

`Codec.FLOAT`

`1.5f`

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#generated-json-file-example)

Generated JSON File Example


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When your plugin runs, it generates a JSON file like this:

Users can edit this file to customize settings, and changes take effect on plugin reload or server restart.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#accessing-config-values)

Accessing Config Values


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#in-your-plugin-class)

In Your Plugin Class:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#from-other-classes)

From Other Classes:

Pass the config or specific values as parameters:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#advanced-list-array-configurations)

Advanced: List/Array Configurations


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For more complex configs with lists or objects, you can use advanced codecs:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#config-reload)

Config Reload


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you want to support config reloading without restarting:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#best-practices)

Best Practices


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#id-1.-use-sensible-defaults)

1\. Use Sensible Defaults

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#id-2.-document-your-config)

2\. Document Your Config

Add comments in your code explaining what each setting does:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#id-3.-validate-values)

3\. Validate Values

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#id-4.-provide-examples)

4\. Provide Examples

Include an example config in your documentation showing all available options.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#config-file-not-generated)

Config file not generated:

*   Verify `withConfig()` is called in plugin constructor
    
*   Check plugin manifest is correct
    
*   Ensure plugin loads successfully (check logs)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#values-not-loading)

Values not loading:

*   Verify JSON syntax is valid
    
*   Check key names match exactly (case-sensitive)
    
*   Ensure data types match codec definitions
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#changes-not-taking-effect)

Changes not taking effect:

*   Restart the server after editing config
    
*   If using reload, ensure reload method is properly implemented
    
*   Check for cached values
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#default-values-not-working)

Default values not working:

*   Verify field initialization: `private double value = 0.40;`
    
*   Check constructor doesn't override defaults
    
*   Ensure codec is built correctly
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/08-custom-config-files#complete-example)

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Copy

    public class ExampleConfig {
    
        // 1. Codec definition for serialization/deserialization
        public static final BuilderCodec<ExampleConfig> CODEC = 
            BuilderCodec.builder(ExampleConfig.class, ExampleConfig::new)
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Double>("LuckIncreaseChance", Codec.DOUBLE),
                        (exConfig, aDouble, extraInfo) -> exConfig.LuckIncreaseChance = aDouble,  // Setter
                        (exConfig, extraInfo) -> exConfig.LuckIncreaseChance)                     // Getter
                .add()
                .build();
    
        // 2. Configuration variable with default value
        private double LuckIncreaseChance = 0.40;
    
        // 3. Constructor
        public ExampleConfig() {
        }
        
        // 4. Getter method (optional but recommended)
        public double getLuckIncreaseChance() {
            return LuckIncreaseChance;
        }
    }

            (exConfig, aDouble, extraInfo) -> exConfig.LuckIncreaseChance = aDouble,  // Setter
            (exConfig, extraInfo) -> exConfig.LuckIncreaseChance)                     // Getter

    .build();

    public class ExamplePlugin extends JavaPlugin {
    
        private final Config<ExampleConfig> config;
    
        public ExamplePlugin(@Nonnull JavaPluginInit init) {
            super(init);
            
            // Registers the configuration with the filename "ExamplePlugin"
            this.config = this.withConfig("ExamplePlugin", ExampleConfig.CODEC);
        }
        
        // Access config values
        public double getLuckChance() {
            return this.config.get().getLuckIncreaseChance();
        }
    }

    public class AdvancedConfig {
    
        public static final BuilderCodec<AdvancedConfig> CODEC = 
            BuilderCodec.builder(AdvancedConfig.class, AdvancedConfig::new)
                // Double field
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Double>("LuckIncreaseChance", Codec.DOUBLE),
                        (config, value, info) -> config.luckIncreaseChance = value,
                        (config, info) -> config.luckIncreaseChance)
                .add()
                
                // Integer field
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Integer>("MaxPlayers", Codec.INT),
                        (config, value, info) -> config.maxPlayers = value,
                        (config, info) -> config.maxPlayers)
                .add()
                
                // String field
                .append(new KeyedCodec<String>("ServerMessage", Codec.STRING),
                        (config, value, info) -> config.serverMessage = value,
                        (config, info) -> config.serverMessage)
                .add()
                
                // Boolean field
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Boolean>("EnableFeature", Codec.BOOL),
                        (config, value, info) -> config.enableFeature = value,
                        (config, info) -> config.enableFeature)
                .add()
                .build();
    
        private double luckIncreaseChance = 0.40;
        private int maxPlayers = 100;
        private String serverMessage = "Welcome!";
        private boolean enableFeature = true;
    
        public AdvancedConfig() {
        }
        
        // Getters
        public double getLuckIncreaseChance() { return luckIncreaseChance; }
        public int getMaxPlayers() { return maxPlayers; }
        public String getServerMessage() { return serverMessage; }
        public boolean isEnableFeature() { return enableFeature; }
    }

      "LuckIncreaseChance": 0.40,
      "MaxPlayers": 100,
      "ServerMessage": "Welcome!",
      "EnableFeature": true
    }

    public class ExamplePlugin extends JavaPlugin {
    
        private final Config<ExampleConfig> config;
    
        public ExamplePlugin(@Nonnull JavaPluginInit init) {
            super(init);
            this.config = this.withConfig("ExamplePlugin", ExampleConfig.CODEC);
        }
    
        public void someMethod() {
            // Access config value
            double luckChance = this.config.get().getLuckIncreaseChance();
            
            // Use the value
            if (Math.random() < luckChance) {
                getLogger().info("Lucky event triggered!");
            }
        }
    }
    

Copy

    public class FeatureManager {
        
        private final double luckChance;
        
        public FeatureManager(double luckChance) {
            this.luckChance = luckChance;
        }
        
        public void checkLuck() {
            if (Math.random() < luckChance) {
                // Do something lucky
            }
        }
    }

    // In your plugin
    FeatureManager manager = new FeatureManager(
        this.config.get().getLuckIncreaseChance()
    );

    public void reloadConfig() {
        // The config automatically reloads from file
        getLogger().info("Config reloaded!");
        
        // Access new values
        double newChance = this.config.get().getLuckIncreaseChance();
        getLogger().info("New luck chance: " + newChance);
    }

    private double luckIncreaseChance = 0.40;  // 40% - balanced default
    

Copy

    // Percentage chance (0.0 to 1.0) for luck increase events
    private double luckIncreaseChance = 0.40;
    

Copy

    public double getLuckIncreaseChance() {
        // Ensure value is between 0 and 1
        return Math.max(0.0, Math.min(1.0, luckIncreaseChance));
    }
    

Copy

    // Config class
    public class MyPluginConfig {
    
        public static final BuilderCodec<MyPluginConfig> CODEC = 
            BuilderCodec.builder(MyPluginConfig.class, MyPluginConfig::new)
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Double>("DropRateMultiplier", Codec.DOUBLE),
                        (cfg, val, info) -> cfg.dropRateMultiplier = val,
                        (cfg, info) -> cfg.dropRateMultiplier)
                .add()
                .append(new KeyedCodec<Boolean>("EnableDebugMode", Codec.BOOL),
                        (cfg, val, info) -> cfg.enableDebugMode = val,
                        (cfg, info) -> cfg.enableDebugMode)
                .add()
                .build();
    
        private double dropRateMultiplier = 1.0;
        private boolean enableDebugMode = false;
    
        public MyPluginConfig() {
        }
    
        public double getDropRateMultiplier() {
            return dropRateMultiplier;
        }
    
        public boolean isDebugMode() {
            return enableDebugMode;
        }
    }
    
    // Plugin class
    public class MyPlugin extends JavaPlugin {
    
        private final Config<MyPluginConfig> config;
    
        public MyPlugin(@Nonnull JavaPluginInit init) {
            super(init);
            this.config = this.withConfig("MyPlugin", MyPluginConfig.CODEC);
            
            // Log loaded values
            getLogger().info("Drop rate multiplier: " + 
                config.get().getDropRateMultiplier());
            getLogger().info("Debug mode: " + 
                config.get().isDebugMode());
        }
    }

# Bootstrap/Early Plugins | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Bootstrap/Early Pluginsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)

**Last Modified:** Friday, January 9, 2026 at 12:01 PM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#important-warning)

Important Warning


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Bootstrap/Early Plugins should only be used when absolutely necessary!**

Early plugins run during a critical phase of the loading process and can significantly impact the game's stability and behavior. Most plugins do NOT need to be early plugins.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#overview)

Overview


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Bootstrap/Early Plugins are a special type of plugin that executes **before** the main Hytale server starts. Their primary function is low-level modification, specifically performing **class transformations** that involve altering or injecting bytecode into classes as they are loaded.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#what-are-early-plugins)

What are Early Plugins?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#key-characteristics)

Key Characteristics:

*   **Execute before main server:** Load during game initialization
    
*   **Outside standard plugin environment:** Cannot access regular plugin APIs
    
*   **No access to:** Event buses, registries, or lifecycle callbacks
    
*   **Primary purpose:** Class transformation and bytecode manipulation
    
*   **High risk:** Can cause stability issues if implemented incorrectly
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#when-to-use-early-plugins)

When to Use Early Plugins:

**Use early plugins for:**

*   Bytecode transformation/modification
    
*   Low-level core game modifications
    
*   Injecting code into existing classes
    
*   Changing fundamental game behavior
    

**Do NOT use early plugins for:**

*   Adding new items, blocks, or mobs (use Packs instead)
    
*   Implementing game features (use regular Plugins)
    
*   Listening to events (use regular Plugins)
    
*   Configuration management (use regular Plugins)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#loading-early-plugins)

Loading Early Plugins


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#default-location)

Default Location:

By default, the game loads early plugins from:

**Important:** You must create this folder manually - the server does not create it automatically.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#custom-locations)

Custom Locations:

Additional paths can be defined using the `--early-plugins` launch argument:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#user-warning-system)

User Warning System


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#warning-message)

Warning Message:

When launching with early plugins installed, users see:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#skipping-the-warning)

Skipping the Warning:

*   **Manual skip:** Press ENTER key
    
*   **Auto-skip:** Add `--accept-early-plugins` launch argument
    
*   **Singleplayer:** Warning is NOT displayed
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#creating-early-plugins)

Creating Early Plugins


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#basic-requirements)

Basic Requirements:

*   Any `.jar` file can be loaded as an early plugin
    
*   **No manifest.json required**
    
*   **No standard entrypoints needed**
    
*   Must implement class transformers via service loader
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#class-transformers)

Class Transformers


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Class transformers allow you to modify the bytecode of classes as they are loaded.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#how-they-work)

How They Work:

1.  Game starts loading classes
    
2.  Before a class is loaded into the JVM
    
3.  Bytes are passed through transformer chain
    
4.  Your transformer modifies the bytes
    
5.  Modified bytes are loaded by JVM
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#step-1-registration)

Step 1: Registration


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Class transformers are loaded using the **Service Loader** pattern:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#id-1.1-create-transformer-class)

1.1 Create Transformer Class:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#id-1.2-create-service-loader-file)

1.2 Create Service Loader File:

**Path:** `src/main/resources/META-INF/services/com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.early.ClassTransformer`

**Contents:**

Add the full qualified name of your transformer class to this file.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#step-2-transformer-priority)

Step 2: Transformer Priority


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Transformers are executed in priority order:

*   **Higher priority** runs BEFORE lower priority
    
*   **Default priority:** 0
    
*   **Negative numbers:** Run later
    
*   **Positive numbers:** Run earlier
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#setting-priority)

Setting Priority:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#priority-examples)

Priority Examples:

*   `100` - Very early (runs first)
    
*   `10` - Early
    
*   `0` - Default (most transformers)
    
*   `-10` - Late
    
*   `-100` - Very late (runs last)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#step-3-restricted-classes)

Step 3: Restricted Classes


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For safety reasons, transformers **cannot modify** classes from certain packages:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#restricted-packages)

Restricted Packages:

*   `java.*`
    
*   `javax.*`
    
*   `jdk.*`
    
*   `sun.*`
    
*   `com.sun.*`
    
*   `org.bouncycastle.*`
    
*   `io.netty.*`
    
*   `org.objectweb.asm.*`
    
*   `com.google.gson.*`
    
*   `org.slf4j.*`
    
*   `org.apache.logging.*`
    
*   `ch.qos.logback.*`
    
*   `com.google.flogger.*`
    
*   `io.sentry.*`
    
*   `com.hypixel.protoplus.*`
    
*   `com.hypixel.fastutil.*`
    
*   `com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.early.*`
    

Attempting to transform these will be ignored or cause errors.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#step-4-writing-transformers)

Step 4: Writing Transformers


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#transform-method)

Transform Method:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#basic-transformation-pattern)

Basic Transformation Pattern:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#example-simple-string-replacement-transformer)

Example: Simple String Replacement Transformer


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This example replaces the startup message with a custom one:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#advanced-using-asm-library)

Advanced: Using ASM Library


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For more complex transformations, use the **ASM library**:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#asm-benefits)

ASM Benefits:

*   Structured bytecode manipulation
    
*   Visitor pattern for class modification
    
*   Less error-prone than raw byte manipulation
    
*   Better maintainability
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#example-asm-transformer)

Example ASM Transformer:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#project-structure)

Project Structure


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#building-early-plugins)

Building Early Plugins


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use Gradle to build:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#best-practices)

Best Practices


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Only use when necessary** - Regular plugins are sufficient for 99% of mods.
    
2.  **Test thoroughly** - Early plugins can break the entire game.
    
3.  **Use ASM or Mixins** - Don't manipulate raw bytes unless you're an expert.
    
4.  **Document transformations** - Explain what you're modifying and why.
    
5.  **Handle errors gracefully** - Return original bytes if transformation fails.
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/09-bootstrap-early-plugins#getting-help)

*   **Blog:** [Hytale Newsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/news)

    @Override
    public byte[] transform(String name, String path, byte[] bytes) {
        // name: Fully qualified class name (e.g., "com.hypixel.hytale.server.HytaleServer")
        // path: File path to the class
        // bytes: Original class bytecode
        
        // Return modified bytes, or original bytes if no changes
        return bytes;
    }
    

Copy

    @Override
    public byte[] transform(String name, String path, byte[] bytes) {
        // Only transform specific class
        if (name.equals("com.hypixel.hytale.server.core.HytaleServer")) {
            // Modify the bytes
            return modifyBytes(bytes);
        }
        
        // Return unchanged for other classes
        return bytes;
    }
    

Copy

    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.early.ClassTransformer;
    import java.nio.ByteBuffer;
    import java.nio.charset.StandardCharsets;
    
    public class ExampleTransformer implements ClassTransformer {
    
        @Override
        public byte[] transform(String name, String path, byte[] bytes) {
            if (name.equals("com.hypixel.hytale.server.core.HytaleServer")) {
                return patchString(bytes, 
                    "Starting HytaleServer", 
                    "Starting Patched HytaleServer >:)");
            }
            return bytes;
        }
    
        public static byte[] patchString(byte[] bytes, String target, String replacement) {
            final byte[] targetBytes = encodeStringWithLength(target);
            final byte[] replacementBytes = encodeStringWithLength(replacement);
            final int index = indexOf(bytes, targetBytes);
            
            if (index == -1) {
                return bytes;  // Target not found
            }
            
            final byte[] result = new byte[bytes.length - targetBytes.length + replacementBytes.length];
            System.arraycopy(bytes, 0, result, 0, index); // Before the target
            System.arraycopy(replacementBytes, 0, result, index, replacementBytes.length); // Replacement
            System.arraycopy(bytes, index + targetBytes.length, result, index + replacementBytes.length, 
                bytes.length - index - targetBytes.length); // After the target
            
            return result;
        }
    
        public static byte[] encodeStringWithLength(String str) {
            final byte[] utf8Bytes = str.getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8);
            ByteBuffer buffer = ByteBuffer.allocate(2 + utf8Bytes.length);
            return buffer.putShort((short) utf8Bytes.length).put(utf8Bytes).array();
        }
    
        private static int indexOf(byte[] array, byte[] target) {
            outer:
            for (int i = 0; i <= array.length - target.length; i++) {
                for (int j = 0; j < target.length; j++) {
                    if (array[i + j] != target[j]) {
                        continue outer;
                    }
                }
                return i;
            }
            return -1;
        }
    }
    

Copy

    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.early.ClassTransformer;
    import org.objectweb.asm.*;
    
    public class AsmTransformer implements ClassTransformer {
    
        @Override
        public byte[] transform(String name, String path, byte[] bytes) {
            if (name.equals("com.example.TargetClass")) {
                ClassReader reader = new ClassReader(bytes);
                ClassWriter writer = new ClassWriter(reader, 0);
                ClassVisitor visitor = new MyClassVisitor(Opcodes.ASM9, writer);
                reader.accept(visitor, 0);
                return writer.toByteArray();
            }
            return bytes;
        }
        
        private static class MyClassVisitor extends ClassVisitor {
            public MyClassVisitor(int api, ClassVisitor cv) {
                super(api, cv);
            }
            
            @Override
            public MethodVisitor visitMethod(int access, String name, 
                    String descriptor, String signature, String[] exceptions) {
                MethodVisitor mv = super.visitMethod(access, name, descriptor, signature, exceptions);
                
                // Modify specific method
                if (name.equals("targetMethod")) {
                    return new MethodModifier(api, mv);
                }
                
                return mv;
            }
        }
        
        private static class MethodModifier extends MethodVisitor {
            public MethodModifier(int api, MethodVisitor mv) {
                super(api, mv);
            }
            
            @Override
            public void visitCode() {
                // Inject code at method start
                super.visitCode();
                // Add your bytecode instructions here
            }
        }
    }

    │       │           └── early/
    │       │               └── ExampleTransformer.java
    │       └── resources/
    │           └── META-INF/
    │               └── services/
    │                   └── com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.early.ClassTransformer
    ├── build.gradle
    └── README.md
    

Copy

    plugins {
        id 'java'
    }
    
    group = 'com.example'
    version = '1.0.0'
    
    repositories {
        mavenCentral()
    }
    
    dependencies {
        // Add Hytale early plugin API
        compileOnly 'com.hypixel.hytale:early-plugin-api:VERSION'
        
        // ASM for bytecode manipulation (optional)
        implementation 'org.ow2.asm:asm:9.5'
        implementation 'org.ow2.asm:asm-commons:9.5'
    }
    
    jar {
        from {
            configurations.runtimeClasspath.collect { 
                it.isDirectory() ? it : zipTree(it) 
            }
        }
    }

# Gradle Automation & Testing | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Last Modified:** Friday, January 10, 2026

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#overview)

Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide covers advanced Gradle automation techniques for Hytale plugin development, including creating custom Gradle tasks for automated server testing and streamlined development workflows.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#custom-gradle-plugin-for-server-testing)

Custom Gradle Plugin for Server Testing


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One of the most time-consuming parts of plugin development is manually:

1.  Building your plugin
    
2.  Copying it to the server's plugins folder
    
3.  Starting the server
    
4.  Testing your changes
    

You can automate this entire workflow with a custom Gradle plugin!

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#creating-a-custom-gradle-plugin)

Creating a Custom Gradle Plugin


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#project-structure)

Project Structure

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-1-create-buildsrc-directory)

Step 1: Create buildSrc Directory

The `buildSrc/` directory is a special Gradle convention for custom build logic.

Create `buildSrc/build.gradle.kts`:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-2-create-the-custom-plugin)

Step 2: Create the Custom Plugin

Create `buildSrc/src/main/kotlin/RunHytalePlugin.kt`:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-3-apply-the-plugin)

Step 3: Apply the Plugin

In your main `build.gradle.kts`:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-4-use-the-task)

Step 4: Use the Task

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#how-it-works)

How It Works


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-1.-smart-caching)

1\. **Smart Caching**

*   Downloads server JAR only once
    
*   Uses SHA-256 hash of URL as cache key
    
*   Subsequent runs use cached version
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-2.-automatic-build)

2\. **Automatic Build**

*   Depends on `shadowJar` task
    
*   Builds your plugin before running
    
*   Copies fresh plugin JAR to server
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-3.-interactive-console)

3\. **Interactive Console**

*   Forwards server output to your terminal
    
*   Allows typing commands directly
    
*   Handles Ctrl+C gracefully
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-4.-clean-workspace)

4\. **Clean Workspace**

*   Server runs in `run/` directory
    
*   Keeps your project root clean
    
*   Easy to delete and reset
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#advanced-gradle-tasks)

* * *

Summary


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#benefits-of-gradle-automation)

Benefits of Gradle Automation:

*   **Faster Development**: One command to build, deploy, and test
    
*   **Consistency**: Same environment every time
    
*   **Efficiency**: Smart caching saves time
    
*   **Professional**: Industry-standard build automation
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#key-tasks-created)

Key Tasks Created:

1.  `runServer` - Build and run server with plugin
    
2.  `quickTest` - Fast compilation checks
    
3.  `cleanRun` - Clean test environment
    
4.  `runServer-{version}` - Test multiple versions

Copy

    import org.gradle.api.DefaultTask
    import org.gradle.api.Plugin
    import org.gradle.api.Project
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.Input
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskAction
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskProvider
    import java.io.File
    import java.net.URI
    import java.security.MessageDigest
    
    // Main plugin class
    open class RunHytalePlugin : Plugin<Project> {
        override fun apply(project: Project) {
            // Create extension for configuration
            val extension = project.extensions.create(
                "runHytale", 
                RunHytaleExtension::class.java
            )
    
            // Register the runServer task
            val runTask: TaskProvider<RunServerTask> = project.tasks.register(
                "runServer", 
                RunServerTask::class.java
            ) {
                jarUrl.set(extension.jarUrl)
                group = "hytale"
                description = "Downloads and runs the Hytale server with your plugin"
            }
    
            // Make runServer depend on shadowJar (build plugin first)
            project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.let {
                runTask.configure {
                    dependsOn(it)
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Extension for configuration
    open class RunHytaleExtension {
        var jarUrl: String = "https://example.com/hytale-server.jar"
    }
    
    // The actual task that runs the server
    open class RunServerTask : DefaultTask() {
    
        @Input
        val jarUrl = project.objects.property(String::class.java)
    
        @TaskAction
        fun run() {
            // Create directories
            val runDir = File(project.projectDir, "run").apply { mkdirs() }
            val pluginsDir = File(runDir, "plugins").apply { mkdirs() }
            val jarFile = File(runDir, "server.jar")
    
            // Cache directory for downloaded server JARs
            val cacheDir = File(
                project.layout.buildDirectory.asFile.get(), 
                "hytale-cache"
            ).apply { mkdirs() }
    
            // Compute hash of URL for caching
            val urlHash = MessageDigest.getInstance("SHA-256")
                .digest(jarUrl.get().toByteArray())
                .joinToString("") { "%02x".format(it) }
            val cachedJar = File(cacheDir, "$urlHash.jar")
    
            // Download server JAR if not cached
            if (!cachedJar.exists()) {
                println("Downloading Hytale server from ${jarUrl.get()}")
                URI.create(jarUrl.get()).toURL().openStream().use { input ->
                    cachedJar.outputStream().use { output ->
                        input.copyTo(output)
                    }
                }
                println("Server JAR downloaded and cached")
            } else {
                println("Using cached server JAR")
            }
    
            // Copy server JAR to run directory
            cachedJar.copyTo(jarFile, overwrite = true)
    
            // Copy plugin JAR to plugins folder
            project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.outputs?.files?.firstOrNull()?.let { shadowJar ->
                val targetFile = File(pluginsDir, shadowJar.name)
                shadowJar.copyTo(targetFile, overwrite = true)
                println("Plugin copied to: ${targetFile.absolutePath}")
            }
    
            println("Starting Hytale server...")
    
            // Start the server process
            val process = ProcessBuilder("java", "-jar", jarFile.name)
                .directory(runDir)
                .start()
    
            // Handle graceful shutdown
            project.gradle.buildFinished {
                if (process.isAlive) {
                    println("Stopping server...")
                    process.destroy()
                }
            }
    
            // Forward stdout to console
            Thread {
                process.inputStream.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach { println(it) }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Forward stderr to console
            Thread {
                process.errorStream.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach { System.err.println(it) }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Forward stdin to server (for commands)
            Thread {
                System.`in`.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach {
                        process.outputStream.write((it + "\n").toByteArray())
                        process.outputStream.flush()
                    }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Wait for server to exit
            val exitCode = process.waitFor()
            println("Server exited with code $exitCode")
        }
    }

        jarUrl = "https://example.com/hytale-server.jar" // Replace with actual URL
    }
    
    // Rest of your build configuration...

    // In buildSrc/src/main/kotlin/DevModeTask.kt
    import org.gradle.api.DefaultTask
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskAction
    import java.nio.file.*
    
    open class DevModeTask : DefaultTask() {
        
        @TaskAction
        fun run() {
            val watchService = FileSystems.getDefault().newWatchService()
            val srcPath = project.file("src/main/java").toPath()
            
            srcPath.register(
                watchService,
                StandardWatchEventKinds.ENTRY_MODIFY,
                StandardWatchEventKinds.ENTRY_CREATE
            )
            
            println("Watching for changes in src/main/java...")
            println("Press Ctrl+C to stop")
            
            while (true) {
                val key = watchService.take()
                
                for (event in key.pollEvents()) {
                    println("Change detected: ${event.context()}")
                    println("Rebuilding plugin...")
                    
                    // Trigger rebuild
                    project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.actions?.forEach { 
                        it.execute(project.tasks.getByName("shadowJar"))
                    }
                    
                    println("Rebuild complete. Copy to server and reload.")
                }
                
                key.reset()
            }
        }
    }

Copy

    tasks.register("quickTest") {
        group = "verification"
        description = "Quick compilation and basic checks"
        
        dependsOn("compileJava")
        
        doLast {
            println("✓ Compilation successful")
            println("✓ No syntax errors")
            
            // Check manifest exists
            val manifest = file("src/main/resources/manifest.json")
            if (manifest.exists()) {
                println("✓ Manifest file found")
            } else {
                throw GradleException("✗ Manifest file missing!")
            }
            
            // Check for common issues
            val srcDir = file("src/main/java")
            srcDir.walk().forEach { file ->
                if (file.extension == "java") {
                    val content = file.readText()
                    
                    // Check for System.out.println (should use logger)
                    if (content.contains("System.out.println")) {
                        println("⚠ Warning: Found System.out.println in ${file.name}")
                        println("  Consider using a logger instead")
                    }
                }
            }
            
            println("\n✓ Quick test passed!")
        }
    }

    org.gradle.parallel=true
    
    # Enable build cache
    org.gradle.caching=true
    
    # Use configuration cache (Gradle 8+)
    org.gradle.configuration-cache=true

    tasks.shadowJar {
        // Minimize JAR size
        minimize()
        
        // Relocate dependencies to avoid conflicts
        relocate("com.google.gson", "com.yourplugin.libs.gson")
        
        // Exclude unnecessary files
        exclude("META-INF/*.SF")
        exclude("META-INF/*.DSA")
        exclude("META-INF/*.RSA")
        
        // Set archive name
        archiveBaseName.set("YourPlugin")
        archiveClassifier.set("")
        archiveVersion.set(project.version.toString())
    }

    // In build.gradle.kts
    val serverVersions = mapOf(
        "latest" to "https://example.com/hytale-latest.jar",
        "stable" to "https://example.com/hytale-stable.jar",
        "beta" to "https://example.com/hytale-beta.jar"
    )
    
    serverVersions.forEach { (name, url) ->
        tasks.register("runServer-$name", RunServerTask::class) {
            group = "hytale"
            description = "Run server with $name version"
            jarUrl.set(url)
        }
    }
    
    // Usage:
    // ./gradlew runServer-latest
    // ./gradlew runServer-stable
    // ./gradlew runServer-beta

        runs-on: ubuntu-latest

            java-version: '25'
            distribution: 'temurin'
        
        - name: Grant execute permission for gradlew
          run: chmod +x gradlew
        
        - name: Build with Gradle
          run: ./gradlew build
        
        - name: Run tests
          run: ./gradlew test
        
        - name: Upload artifact
          uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
          with:
            name: plugin-jar
            path: build/libs/*.jar

        .directory(runDir)

# Getting Started with Plugins | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Getting Started with Pluginsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)

**Last Modified:** Friday, January 16, 2026 at 07:30 AM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#overview)

Overview


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide will help you get started with creating **Plugins** for Hytale. Plugins are mods written in **Java** that use the game's API to expand vanilla functionality and add new content programmatically.

> **Early Access Warning**: The game Hytale is in early access, and so is this project! Features may be incomplete, unstable, or change frequently. Please be patient and understanding as development continues.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before you begin, ensure you have:

*   **Hytale** installed via the official launcher
    
*   **IntelliJ IDEA** (Community Edition is fine)
    
*   **Java 25** downloaded and configured
    
*   Basic **Java programming** knowledge
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-1-download-the-idea-template)

Step 1: Download the IDEA Template


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The easiest way to start developing plugins is by using the official template created by **Darkhax & Jared**.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#plugin-template)

Plugin Template:

*   **Hytale Plugin Template:** [Github Repoarrow-up-right](https://github.com/realBritakee/hytale-template-plugin)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#template-features)

Template Features:

The template includes many great features:

*   Adds the latest Hytale server files to your classpath
    
*   Run the game from your IDE with breakpoint support
    
*   Bundle assets with your plugin (editable with in-game Asset Editor)
    
*   Supports various patch lines (releases and pre-releases)
    
*   Includes example code and assets
    
*   Pre-configured Gradle build system
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-2-configure-the-template-before-importing)

Step 2: Configure the Template Before Importing


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

> **Important:** Configure the project before importing it into IDEA to avoid caching issues later.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.1-extract-the-template)

2.1 Extract the Template

1.  Download the ZIP file from the GitHub repository
    
2.  Extract contents to your desired development location
    
3.  Read the included `README.md` for detailed setup instructions
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.2-configure-project-files)

2.2 Configure Project Files

Before importing the project, you need to configure three key files:

#### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-1.-set-project-name-in-settings.gradle)

1\. Set Project Name in `settings.gradle`

Set the name of your project. Use capitalized names and avoid whitespace and special characters, as this will be used as the base name for files produced by Gradle (like the JAR file).

#### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.-review-gradle-properties-in-gradle.properties)

2\. Review Gradle Properties in `gradle.properties`

Update the properties to match your project:

#### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.-update-manifest-file-in-src-main-resources-manifest.json)

3\. Update Manifest File in `src/main/resources/manifest.json`

The manifest file provides important information about your plugin to Hytale. Update every property to reflect your project:

**Important Manifest Properties:**

*   **Main**: The most critical property - tells the game which class file to load as the entry point for your plugin
    
*   **Version** and **IncludesAssetPack**: These are automatically updated by Gradle during development and builds, allowing you to use the in-game asset editor
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-3-import-the-project-into-idea)

Step 3: Import the Project into IDEA


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Launch IntelliJ IDEA**
    
2.  **Open Project:**
    

*   Click `File` -> `Open`
    
*   Navigate to your extracted and configured template folder
    
*   Select the folder and click `OK`
    

1.  **Wait for Initialization:**
    

*   IDEA will automatically import the Gradle project
    
*   The `HytaleServer` run configuration will be created automatically
    
*   A `./run` folder will be generated
    
*   Dependencies will be downloaded automatically
    
*   This may take several minutes on first run
    

> **Note:** If you don't see the `HytaleServer` run configuration, open the dropdown menu or click "Edit Configurations..." once to unhide it.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-4-configure-java-25-sdk)

Step 4: Configure Java 25 SDK


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you haven't already added Java 25 as an SDK:

1.  **Open Project Structure:**
    

*   `File` -> `Project Structure` (or `Ctrl+Alt+Shift+S`)
    

1.  **Add SDK:**
    

*   Click `SDKs` under `Platform Settings`
    
*   Click `+` -> `Add JDK`
    
*   Navigate to your Java 25 installation
    
*   Click `OK`
    

1.  **Set Project SDK:**
    

*   Go to `Project` settings
    
*   Set `SDK` to Java 25
    
*   Click `Apply` and `OK`
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-5-understanding-the-project-structure)

Step 5: Understanding the Project Structure


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-6-authenticating-your-test-server)

Step 6: Authenticating Your Test Server


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

> **CRITICAL:** You MUST authenticate your test server before you can connect to it!

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#initial-authentication)

Initial Authentication

1.  Run the server once from IDEA (it will start but you won't be able to connect yet)
    
2.  In the server terminal, run:
    

1.  The command will print a URL
    
2.  Open the URL in your browser and authenticate using your Hytale account
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#persistent-authentication)

Persistent Authentication

After authenticating once, run this command to keep your server authenticated after restarting:

> **Security Warning:** Never share your encrypted auth file with anyone!

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#alternative-authenticate-from-code)

Alternative: Authenticate from Code

If you're unable to run commands from the IDEA terminal, you can authenticate from code:

**Important:** Remove this code after your server is authenticated!

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-7-running-the-game-from-idea)

Step 7: Running the Game from IDEA


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#using-the-pre-configured-run-configuration)

Using the Pre-configured Run Configuration

1.  **Select Run Configuration:**
    

*   Look for the dropdown in the top-right of IDEA
    
*   Select `HytaleServer`
    

1.  **Run or Debug:**
    

*   Click the green play button to run
    
*   Click the bug button to debug with breakpoints
    

1.  **Server Starts:**
    

*   Hytale server will start with your plugin loaded
    
*   Default assets from the game will be loaded into the `./run` folder
    
*   You can set breakpoints in your code
    
*   Debug console shows plugin output
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#connecting-to-your-local-server)

Connecting to Your Local Server

Once the server is running:

1.  **Launch the standard Hytale client** (not from IDEA)
    
2.  **Connect to Local Server:**
    

*   The server should appear automatically
    
*   If it doesn't, manually add the IP: `127.0.0.1`
    

1.  **Join the server** to test your plugin
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-8-verifying-the-example-plugin)

Step 8: Verifying the Example Plugin


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The template includes an example plugin you can use to verify everything is working:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#test-command)

Test Command

Run the `/test` command in-game. It will print the name and version of your plugin.

> **Note:** This is for demonstration purposes and should be removed before your final release.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#example-recipe)

Example Recipe

The example plugin includes a recipe that allows you to craft 10 dirt into 1 dirt using the crafting window. This demonstrates how assets can be bundled with your plugin.

> **Note:** This example should also be removed before release.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-9-building-your-plugin)

Step 9: Building Your Plugin


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create a shareable JAR file of your plugin:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#build-with-gradle)

Build with Gradle

**Option 1: Terminal**

**Option 2: IDEA Gradle Panel**

1.  Open the Gradle panel (right side of IDEA)
    
2.  Navigate to: `Tasks` -> `build` -> `build`
    
3.  Double-click `build`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#output-location)

Output Location

Your plugin JAR will be located at:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-10-installing-plugins-in-hytale)

Step 10: Installing Plugins in Hytale


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#installation-path)

Installation Path

**Full Path (Windows):**

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#installation-steps)

Installation Steps

1.  **Create Mods Folder** (if it doesn't exist)
    
2.  **Copy your plugin JAR** into the `Mods/` folder
    
3.  **Launch Hytale**
    
4.  Your plugin will be loaded automatically
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#alternative-ide-support)

Alternative IDE Support


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#using-vscode)

Using VSCode

While VSCode is not officially supported, you can generate launch configurations by running:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#example-plugin-code)

Example Plugin Code


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here's a basic plugin structure:

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#plugin-development-tips)

Plugin Development Tips


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-1.-use-the-logger)

1\. Use the Logger

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.-register-event-listeners)

2\. Register Event Listeners

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.-access-the-api)

3\. Access the API

The template includes Hytale's API in the classpath:

*   Explore the API through IntelliJ's autocomplete
    
*   Check the example code included in the template
    
*   Browse available classes and methods
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-4.-bundle-assets)

4\. Bundle Assets

You can include Packs (assets) with your Plugin:

*   Add assets to `src/main/resources/Common/` and `Server/`
    
*   They'll be bundled with your plugin JAR
    
*   Editable in-game via the Asset Editor
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#debugging-tips)

Debugging Tips


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#breakpoints)

Breakpoints

1.  Click in the left margin next to a line number
    
2.  A red dot appears indicating a breakpoint
    
3.  Run in Debug mode (bug icon)
    
4.  Execution pauses at breakpoints
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#console-output)

Console Output

*   Plugin logs appear in the IDEA console
    
*   Use `getLogger()` for clean output
    
*   Check for error stack traces
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#hot-reload)

Hot Reload

*   Some changes can be reloaded without restarting
    
*   Rebuild the project (`Ctrl+F9`)
    
*   Major changes require a full restart
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#gradle-sync-fails)

Gradle sync fails

*   Check internet connection (downloads dependencies)
    
*   Verify Java 25 is properly installed
    
*   Try: `./gradlew clean build`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#hytaleserver-run-config-missing)

HytaleServer run config missing

*   Re-import Gradle project
    
*   Check `build.gradle` for run configuration setup
    
*   Open the run configuration dropdown or click "Edit Configurations..." to unhide it
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#plugin-doesnt-load)

Plugin doesn't load

*   Verify `manifest.json` is correct (especially the `Main` property)
    
*   Check logs for error messages
    
*   Ensure plugin JAR is in correct Mods folder
    
*   Confirm Hytale version compatibility
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#cannot-connect-to-local-server)

Cannot connect to local server

*   Ensure you've authenticated the server with `auth login device`
    
*   Verify the server is running (check IDEA console)
    
*   Try manually adding IP: `127.0.0.1`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#breakpoints-dont-work)

Breakpoints don't work

*   Ensure you're running in Debug mode (bug icon)
    
*   Verify breakpoint is in executed code
    
*   Check that source code matches compiled JAR
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#getting-help)

Getting Help


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Official Channels:**

*   **Discord:** [Official Hytale Discordarrow-up-right](https://discord.gg/hytale)
    
*   **Blog:** [Hytale Newsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/news)

Copy

    rootProject.name = 'your-plugin-name'
    

Copy

    # Change maven_group to match your project
    maven_group = com.yourname
    # Update version before making new releases
    version = 1.0.0
    # ... other properties
    

Copy

    {
      "Group": "com.yourname",
      "Name": "YourPluginName",
      "Main": "com.yourname.yourplugin.YourPlugin",
      "Version": "1.0.0",
      "Description": "Description of your plugin",
      "Authors": [\
        {\
          "Name": "Your Name",\
          "Email": "your.email@example.com",\
          "Url": "https://your-website.com"\
        }\
      ],
      "Website": "https://your-plugin-website.com",
      "ServerVersion": "*",
      "Dependencies": {},
      "OptionalDependencies": {},
      "DisabledByDefault": false
    }
    

Copy

    your-plugin-name/
    |-- src/
    |   `-- main/
    |       |-- java/
    |       |   `-- com/
    |       |       `-- yourname/
    |       |           `-- yourplugin/
    |       |               `-- YourPlugin.java
    |       `-- resources/
    |           |-- manifest.json
    |           |-- Common/          # Assets (models, textures)
    |           `-- Server/          # Server-side data
    |-- build.gradle
    |-- settings.gradle
    |-- gradle.properties
    |-- README.md
    `-- run/                         # Generated when you run the server
    

Copy

    auth login device
    

Copy

    auth persistence Encrypted
    

Copy

    @Override
    protected void start() {
        CommandManager.get().handleCommand(ConsoleSender.INSTANCE, "auth login device");
    }
    

Copy

    ./gradlew build
    

Copy

    build/libs/your-plugin-name-1.0.0.jar
    

Copy

    %appdata%/Hytale/UserData/Mods/
    

Copy

    C:\Users\YourUsername\AppData\Roaming\Hytale\UserData\Mods\
    

Copy

    ./gradlew generateVSCodeLaunch
    

Copy

    package com.yourname.yourplugin;
    
    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.JavaPlugin;
    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.JavaPluginInit;
    import javax.annotation.Nonnull;
    
    public class YourPlugin extends JavaPlugin {
    
        public YourPlugin(@Nonnull JavaPluginInit init) {
            super(init);
            
            // Plugin initialization code
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin has been loaded!");
        }
    
        @Override
        public void onEnable() {
            // Called when plugin is enabled
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin enabled!");
        }
    
        @Override
        public void onDisable() {
            // Called when plugin is disabled
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin disabled!");
        }
    }
    

Copy

    getLogger().info("Information message");
    getLogger().warn("Warning message");
    getLogger().error("Error message");
    

Copy

    getServer().getPluginManager().registerEvents(new MyListener(), this);
